# Text Elements
                A driver makes a turn.
The inertial force prevents them from moving forward 
and cracking their skull. ^93qe0toH

This inertial force is fictitious,
It seems real, but only because
the observer's frame of reference 
  is rotating or accelerating ^O5vfbbc9

1. The force of gravity is negligible ^XjldRG37

2. The force of tension will head 
   to the center ^U4gRe0Nj

1. The only time this system is undergoing
  UCM is when the force to keep the system
  up is enough to counteract the force of
  gravity ^7CXNefcx

2. The force of gravity would be 0 ^S0vZKDMP

v ^l6FHd6fl

If a car wants to make a turn, 
there is a certain velocity (lets call it v   )
that a car needs to be at to successfully 
make the turn with UCM.

In these cases of UCM, friction does not need to act.

However, if the car moves quicker or slower than     ,
Friction will have to act to assist in the turn. ^hQdjkw9S

If v < v ^l9Lr7c9R

ideal ^XDCidu98

Centripetal Force is smaller ^Gw6MI7m0

Friction acts up the slope. It combats acceleration ^TB2a4rci

Friction ^p1NNHfHg

Friction ^BnH17RjQ

On a banked curve,
an object does not need Friction to make a turn.
This is because the curve is already on an incline ^wSD5S5tb

Instead, what allows the object to turn
is the Normal Force ^Kua7YcVp
